<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Saleen</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Saleen Automotive</b>, commonly known as <b>Saleen</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">manufacturer</a> of specialty high-performance <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">sports cars</a> and high-performance automotive parts. Saleen is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Corona,_California" title="Corona, California">Corona, California</a>, USA. On June 26, 2013 Saleen Automotive, Inc became <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a> through a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reverse_merger" title="Reverse merger">reverse merger</a>. It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/OTC_Bulletin_Board" title="OTC Bulletin Board">OTC Bulletin Board</a> and is controlled and majority owned by Saleen brand founder <a href="/wiki/Steve_Saleen" title="Steve Saleen">Steve Saleen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Saleen's flagship car is the <a href="/wiki/Saleen_S7" title="Saleen S7">Saleen S7</a>, introduced in 2000. The S7 was wholly built by Saleen and features a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-engine" title="Mid-engine">mid-engine</a> design in a high-performance <a href="/wiki/Supercar" title="Supercar">supercar</a> package. It is also currently the only Saleen production car not based on an existing design or <a href="/wiki/Chassis" title="Chassis">chassis</a>.</p>
<p>Saleen currently manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Saleen_302_Series" title="Saleen 302 Series">S302</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang#Fifth_generation_.282005.E2.80.932014.29" title="Ford Mustang">Mustang</a>-based), S620 (<a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Camaro#Fifth_generation:_2010.E2.80.93present" title="Chevrolet Camaro">Camaro</a>-based), the S570 (<a href="/wiki/Dodge_Challenger#Third_generation_.282008.E2.80.93present.29" title="Dodge Challenger">Challenger</a>-based), and the GTX (<a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a>-based), and most recently have announced that they are in development of a new Saleen supercar, a limited run successor to the S7 supercar, the S7 LM.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Saleen <a href="/wiki/Brand" title="Brand">brand</a> was established in 1983 originally as <b>Saleen Autosport</b> by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Saleen" title="Steve Saleen">Steve Saleen</a>, a former professional <a href="/wiki/Formula_Atlantic" title="Formula Atlantic">Formula Atlantic</a> race car driver. The 1st Saleen was produced in 1984 when they built 3 cars as the first production run – a white hatchback, a copper glow hatchback, and a black hatchback.</p>
<p>In 1985, Steve Saleen put the first certified <a href="/wiki/Supercharger" title="Supercharger">supercharger</a> on a production Saleen Mustang. This car was delivered to Nault Ford in <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester, NH</a> and was the first use of a <a href="/wiki/Centrifugal-type_supercharger" title="Centrifugal-type supercharger">centrifugal</a> supercharger on the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fox_platform" title="Ford Fox platform">late model Mustang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1986, the Saleen made its entry into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCCA" title="SCCA">Sport Car Club of America</a> Race Series with a race prepped version of the Saleen Mustang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> A notable win that year at the grueling 24 Hours of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mosport_Park" title="Mosport Park">Mosport</a> was the catalyst for Saleen vehicles becoming heavily involved in motorsport throughout the rest of the 1980s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By 1990, in response to increased aftermarket parts demand, Saleen established <a href="#Saleen_Performance_Parts">Saleen Performance Parts</a> as an independent operation.</p>
<p>In 1994, Saleen debuted the S351 which touted a Saleen built 351ci engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Despite the Mustang GT changing to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_modular_engine" title="Ford modular engine">modular V8</a> in 1996, Saleen continued with development of their own EPA-certified 351W engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, Steve Saleen teamed up with comedian <a href="/wiki/Tim_Allen" title="Tim Allen">Tim Allen</a> and formed the <b>Saleen-Allen “RRR” Speedlab</b> race team.</p>
<p>In 1997, Saleen introduced a Saleen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_Contour" title="Ford Contour">Contour</a> concept and an SUV, the <a href="/wiki/Saleen_XP8" title="Saleen XP8">Saleen XP8</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Explorer#Second_generation_.281995.E2.80.932001.29" title="Ford Explorer">Explorer</a>.</p>
<p>In the late 1990s, the company was <a href="/wiki/Restructuring" title="Restructuring">restructured</a> and became <b>Saleen, Inc.</b>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Saleen introduced their flagship vehicle, the <a href="/wiki/Saleen_S7" title="Saleen S7">Saleen S7</a> supercar. The S7 is a mid-engine, high-performance sports car that was initially priced at just under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>400,000. The S7 won four different GT championships in 2001 and has broken records at the prestigious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/24_hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 hours of Le Mans">24-Hour Le Mans</a> race. The S7 was Saleen's only production car not based on an existing design or chassis.</p>
<p>In 2001, Saleen moved its production facilities to a new 100,000 square foot facility in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irvine,_CA" title="Irvine, CA">Irvine, CA</a>, USA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, Saleen was awarded the assembly and paint contract for the new Ford supercar, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT" title="Ford GT">Ford GT</a>. This effectively made Saleen a Tier 1 supplier to <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, Saleen set up a special manufacturing and licensing agreement for distribution of Saleen vehicles in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, Saleen expanded its operations and manufacturing to an additional 203,000 square foot facility in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Troy,_MI" title="Troy, MI">Troy, MI</a>, USA. The new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/$" title="$">$</a>15<a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">M</a> production facility included a high-tech paint facility and assembly line where Saleen produced the Ford GT under contract from Ford Motor Company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, global distribution was expanded to include <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> under a new partnership with a <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> based importer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Saleen opened its first own branded retail store in an outdoor shopping center in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. The showroom was described as a unique shopping experience for Saleen vehicles, parts, and apparel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Saleen began working with <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> and supplied all the paint work for the new <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Viper#Fourth_generation.2C_Phase_II_ZB_.282008.E2.80.932010.29" title="Dodge Viper">Dodge Viper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Saleen entered into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merger" title="Merger">merger</a> that resulted in Saleen being a publicly traded company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Later that year it was announced that the Saleen operations, manufacturing, <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">R&amp;D</a>, and paint facilities would be consolidated to an expansive four acre campus in Southern California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Saleen entered into an agreement to expand vehicle distribution to include China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In August 2014, Saleen unveiled an all-electric performance model, the FOURSIXTEEN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, There has been much talk among Saleen fans about the possibility of an all electric version of Saleen's signature car, the almighty S7. There has been speculation that an electric version, being dubbed 'S7E', could possibly be under development utilizing drivetrain and electronics from the Tesla Model S platform. It has been noted that Saleen has previous experience with the Model S platform, in their modified version the Saleen GTX (Previously named the FOURSIXTEEN), which Saleen offers in their current product lineup. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Vehicles">Special Vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Special Vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>These are special vehicles made by Saleen, that were either non-production models, concept vehicles, or non-serialized versions.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th style="width: 75px;">Year</th>
<th>Model</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1986</th>
<td>Ford Tempo</td>
<td>Concept</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1988</th>
<td>Special Service Saleens</td>
<td>This was a run of 14 vehicles that Saleen built for Damerow Ford, in <a href="/wiki/Beaverton,_Oregon" title="Beaverton, Oregon">Beaverton, Oregon</a>. The dealership purchased the vehicles as Special Service Vehicles for law enforcement. Rather than selling them to the state, Damerow sent them to Saleen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1989–1990</th>
<td>California Edition GT by Saleen</td>
<td>Non-serialized. This was a run of 50 vehicles for Ford. These were built at Sears Point Raceway and picked up by the dealers from there.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1989</th>
<td>Seal Beach Police Car</td>
<td>In 1989, Saleen was approached by the Seal Beach Police Department to create a vehicle that had the power, suspension, and braking that would give them an edge in pursuits. Only one car was ever made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1989</th>
<td>Eagle One Giveaway Cars</td>
<td>In 1989 and 1990, Eagle One purchased two special-order Saleen hatchbacks each year that were used as promotional vehicles. One was given away to a randomly picked customer, the other to the highest-selling employee of the Chief Auto Parts chain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1992–1993</th>
<td>GT Sport by Steve Saleen</td>
<td>Non-serialized</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1993</th>
<td>RRR</td>
<td>This was a one-off S302 that was built for actor, comedian, and Saleen driver Tim Allen.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1994</th>
<td>V-6 Sport by Steve Saleen</td>
<td>In 1994, Saleen wanted to offer an "entry level" car that combined traditional Saleen equipment with a less-expensive powerplant. This model came with a supercharged V-6 that was rated at 220 hp.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1996</th>
<td>Ford Windstar</td>
<td>The Saleen Windstar was another one-off vehicle built special for Tim Allen.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>1999</th>
<td>Ford Contour</td>
<td>Concept</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2002–2004</th>
<td>Saleen/Bonspeed Thunderbird</td>
<td>Bonspeed and Saleen teamed up to build a special edition Thunderbird. Only three were produced before the project was canceled.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2004</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang_variants#2004_Mustang_GT-R_Concept" title="Ford Mustang variants">Ford Mustang GT-R</a></td>
<td>The Ford Mustang GT-R Concept was produced by Saleen Special Vehicles in <a href="/wiki/Troy,_Michigan" title="Troy, Michigan">Troy, Michigan</a>. It was unveiled at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_International_Auto_Show" title="New York International Auto Show">New York Auto Show</a> by Kid Rock.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2007</th>
<td>Bumblebee and Barricade</td>
<td>Saleen was responsible for build both the hero car, <a href="/wiki/Bumblebee_(Transformers)" title="Bumblebee (Transformers)">Bumblebee</a>, and the villain car, <a href="/wiki/Barricade_(Transformers)" title="Barricade (Transformers)">Barricade</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Transformers_(film)" title="Transformers (film)">the movie, <i>Transformers</i></a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2007–2008</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ford_F-Series#Harley-Davidson_Edition" title="Ford F-Series">Harley-Davidson Edition Ford F-150</a></td>
<td>Saleen Troy produced the HD F-150 S/C for Ford Motor Company. The Supercharged option features a Saleen Series VI supercharger, a dual stage water-to-air intercooler, 39 lb. fuel injectors, a high flow inlet tube, Saleen “Powerflash” performance calibration, and a performance air filter.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2007–2008</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Saleen_S5S_Raptor" title="Saleen S5S Raptor">S5S Raptor</a></td>
<td>This was a concept vehicle intended as a competitor to the Lamborghini Gallardo as well as a follow-on project to the Ford GT. Priced below $200k, the Saleen S5S Raptor was positioned to compete with the best entry level exotics from Ferrari, Lamborghini and Aston Martin.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>2008–2009</th>
<td>Sleeper GT S/C</td>
<td>The Sleeper Edition program was a means to liquidate Mustang GTs that were for Gurney conversion. These were Vista Blue and Performance White coupes.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saleen_Performance_Parts">Saleen Performance Parts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Saleen Performance Parts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The aftermarket parts department of the company markets car parts and accessories such as custom wheels, exhaust systems, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brakes" title="Brakes">brakes</a>, and other high-performance parts.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superchargers" title="Superchargers">Superchargers</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Series I – This was the first supercharger system created by Saleen. It was engineered with an <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Corporation" title="Eaton Corporation">Eaton</a> <a href="/wiki/Roots-type_supercharger" title="Roots-type supercharger">Roots-type supercharger</a> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>Series II – Launched in 2001, the Series II supercharger was a newer generation Eaton M90 roots-type.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li>Series III – This was a larger version of the Eaton supercharger. Going from 90 ci of displacement to 112 ci.</li>
<li>Series IV – The Series IV switched from a roots-type supercharger to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotary_screw_compressor" title="Rotary screw compressor">twin screw-type</a>. This version had 1.6L of displacement.</li>
<li>Series V – This marked the first forced-induction system developed entirely in-house by Saleen and designed around Lysholm-sourced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotary_screw_compressor" title="Rotary screw compressor">compressor screws</a> with 2.3L of displacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li>Series VI – This was very similar to the Series V supercharger with added boost pressure producing more horsepower. This supercharger system was available in versions for the 2005-2009 Ford Mustang, the 2004-2008 Ford F-150 5.4L truck, Ford Expedition, Lincoln Mark LT, and Lincoln Navigator.</li>
<li>Saleen Shakercharger – A ram-air intake system for the Ford Mustang incorporating the Saleen Series VI supercharger with a functional hood scoop system borrowing its appearance from the S302PJ. This product was the result of design collaboration among Saleen's engineering interns in 2007 and 2008.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a> adapter</b> – a factory-installed option that was available across all of Saleen's products line that provides for an integrated iPod connection to the radio head unit. Saleen also offered this option as an aftermarket-installed product through their Speedlabs division.</li>
<li><b>2005–2009 Mustang <a href="/wiki/High-intensity_discharge_lamp" title="High-intensity discharge lamp">HID</a> headlamps</b> – OEM, DOT approved bi-xenon headlamps offered by Saleen that fit 2005-2009 Mustangs. As of early 2007, these were the only OEM-grade, street-legal HID headlamps available for the Ford Mustang</li>
<li><b>Saleen Mustang Scenic Roof</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> – Available across Saleen's Mustang-based products, this comprises a glass full-roof panel that replaces the traditional mustang coupe roof in lieu of a sunroof option. The scenic roof was manufactured from tempered laminate glass and fully certified according to U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) standards.
<ul>
<li><b>Frost Touch Scenic Roof</b> – This is a version of the scenic roof that contains <a href="/wiki/Smart_glass" title="Smart glass">Smart glass</a>. This glass has the ability to change from clear to opaque by flipping a switch.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Watt%27s_linkage" title="Watt's linkage">Watt's Link</a></b> – Developed in 2007, Saleen designed a version of the popular Watt's link for 2005-2009 Ford Mustangs.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colorlab_Automotive_Paints">Colorlab Automotive Paints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Colorlab Automotive Paints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the development of the Saleen SR in year 1995, Saleen formed a strategic partnership with <a href="/wiki/BASF" title="BASF">BASF</a> that resulted in the development of unique paint color formulations coupled with advertising centered around Saleen products. During this time, the Saleen paint color "Mystic" was formulated which gave the color a chameleoon-like effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Shortly after, an updated color called "Rainbow" was released as an evolved version of the "Mystic" color which gave a more chameleon-like effect by displaying more color changes.</p>
<p>Since this time, the Saleen paint color Liztick Red Metallic, named for Steve's wife, Liz, was developed along with twelve more colors, including two named for Steve's daughter, Molly Saleen, Mollypop Pink and Chrome Molly. Other Saleen exclusive colors include Plum Insane Metallic, Burnout Black Pearl, Tire Smoke White Pearl, Sour Apple Green Metallic, Orange County Orange Metallic, Maliblue Metallic, Speedlab Yellow, Shark Skin Metallic, and Beryllium Copper Metallic, and California Sunset Metallic.</p>
<p>In 2014, Saleen signed and agreement that made BASF the exclusive paint supplier for Saleen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Motorsport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Saleen S7R driven by Sascha Bert</div>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg/220px-Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg/330px-Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg/440px-Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saleen_S7R_Race.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Saleen S7R of ACEMCO Motorsports at 2004 Petit Le Mans</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Saleen's birth year of 1984 also marked the first year that a Saleen Mustang was entered into a race, when owner, Steve Saleen, introduced the first streetcar, the Saleen Mustang, and raced it at <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_Raceway" title="Sonoma Raceway">Sears Point Raceway, California</a>.</p>
<p>In 1986, Saleen entered the <a href="/wiki/Sports_Car_Club_of_America" title="Sports Car Club of America">Sports Car Club of America</a> (SCCA) Endurance Series with a race prepared version of the Saleen Mustang, winning the grueling 24 Hours of Mosport, Canada with a sponsorship from General Tire.</p>
<p>1987 brought an SCCA Drivers' Championship to Saleen. The Saleen 3-car team with drivers Steve Saleen, Parnelli Jones, and George Follmer also captured the Team, Manufacturer, and Tire Championships, with sponsorship from General Tire. Saleen entered the SCCA Endurance Series with an all-female driving team including Desire Wilson and Lisa Cacares who obtained the team's 1st victory of the season at Sears Point, California. Saleen Autosport also entered a General Tire backed, Ford Ranger-based, Saleen Sportruck in the SCCA Race Truck Challenge, where they captured two wins.</p>
<p>In 1988, the Saleen race team finished 1st, 2nd, and 3rd at 24 Hours of Mosport for the third consecutive win and gives Ford its first 1-2-3 finish since LeMans in the late 1960s.</p>
<p>1989 was a busy year for the Saleen race team. They entered the PPG Indy Car World Series with a team backed by Montgomery Ward. Saleen Mustangs and Sportrucks also continued their winning campaigns in SCCA Competition with General Tire sponsorship.</p>
<p>In 1990, Saleen entered the SCCA Trans-Am series with a Saleen Mustang backed by General Tire.</p>
<p>Adding to their wins, in 1991 Saleen won the SCCA Race Truck championship with five victories in six races which moved Saleen into a tie for the most victories in the series (49) and the Manufacturers' Championship. Owner and driver, Steve Saleen, campaigned the Trans-Am series with Saleen Mustang with sponsorship from Champion Batteries.</p>
<p>Saleen returned to SCCA Endurance competition in 1993 with a supercharged Saleen in the World Challenge Series.</p>
<p>In 1995, Saleen formed the Saleen/Allen "RRR" Speedlab with Tim Allen. The team of Steve Saleen, Tim Allen, and Bob Bondurant set new track records and won the final race of the SCCA World Challenge series.</p>
<p>For 1996, The Saleen/Allen "RRR" Speedlab, with teammates Steve Saleen and Tim Allen won the SCCA Manufacturers’ Championship with the SR Widebody Saleen Mustang. Saleen also won at <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Glen_International" title="Watkins Glen International">Watkins Glen International</a> Raceway.</p>
<p>In 1997, Saleen/Allen "RRR" Speedlab competed at 24 Hours of Le Mans for the first time, marking the Mustang's first return in over 30 years. Saleen also clinched the SCCA Manufacturers’ Championship title for the third time.</p>
<p>1998 brought more wins for the Saleen/Allen "RRR" Speedlab. The team won both the SCCA Manufacturers' and Drivers' Championship titles.</p>
<p>Come 1999, an ex-LeMans Saleen SR won the Spanish FIA GT championship.</p>
<p>In 2000, Saleen competed in the inaugural Grand American Road Racing season, Saleen captured the Drivers' Championship and clinched the Manufacturers' and Team Championships in the season finale at Watkins Glen International Raceway. Saleen customer cars participated in the <a href="/wiki/Pirelli_World_Challenge" title="Pirelli World Challenge">Speedvision World Challenge</a>—earning a victory at Lime Rock Park.</p>
<p>For the 2001 race season, the racing version of the S7, the Saleen S7R, was introduced. The S7R dominated racetracks during its inaugural season. Saleen S7R customer teams won four Drivers’ Championships in four different series (American LeMans, European LeMans, Grand Am, and Spanish GT). Teams driving the S7R achieved 19 wins out of 32 races including the 12 Hours of Sebring. The S7R grabbed 27 poles and set 27 fastest laps, at many tracks, including the prestigious 24 Hours of LeMans.</p>
<p>2002 brought more victories for the S7R. Customer teams continued to operate in four series (American LeMans, Grand Am, British GT, and Spanish GT) winning 18 out of 40 races, three Drivers’ Championships, and several more Team and Manufacturers' Championships. It also won 21 poles and set 23 fastest laps.</p>
<p>In 2004, while Europe watched, the Saleen S7R captured the 1st place win at <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Enzo_e_Dino_Ferrari" title="Autodromo Enzo e Dino Ferrari">Imola, Italy</a>, beating home-track favorites Ferrari, Maserati, and Lamborghini, and the debuting Maserati MC-12.</p>
<p>In 2006 the Saleen/Oreca Race Team drove the S7 race version and captured the fastest lap and took the victory at <a href="/wiki/Circuit_de_Spa-Francorchamps" title="Circuit de Spa-Francorchamps">Circuit de Spa-Francorchamps</a>. Saleen also began support of formula race teams in Europe. S7 racecars and spare parts were donated to the effort of trying to win on the European circuit.</p>
<p><br/></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="OEM_Development">OEM Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saleen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: OEM Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Beginning in 2002 and at the request of Ford Motor Company, Saleen was highly instrumental in the design, development and assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT" title="Ford GT">Ford GT</a>.</p>
<p>Beginning with the 2007 model year, the Saleen-designed 450 hp (340 kW) supercharger kit in the F-150-based S331 was offered by Ford as a ship-through Ford-endorsed performance option on Harley Davidson Edition F150s.</p>
<p>At the 2007 New York International Auto Show, Chip Foose unveiled a Ford-endorsed limited edition F150, powered by the Saleen-designed powertrain used on the Saleen S331SC.</p>
